Chem. Res.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">50</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2642</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">2652</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.accounts.7b00402</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D50%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D2642-2652%26journal%3DAcc.%2BChem.%2BRes.%26author%3DY.%2BShi%26author%3DX.%2BZhou%26author%3DG.%2BYu%26title%3DMaterial%2Band%2BStructural%2BDesign%2Bof%2BNovel%2BBinder%2BSystems%2Bfor%2BHigh%2BEnergy%252C%2BHigh-Power%2BLithium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.accounts.7b00402&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.7b08714&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.accounts.7b00402&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Material and Structural Design of Novel Binder Systems for High-Energy, High-Power Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi, Ye; Zhou, Xingyi; Yu, Guihua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">50</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2642-2652</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACHRE4</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0001-4842</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Developing high-performance battery systems requires the optimization of every battery component, from electrodes and electrolyte to binder systems.  However, the conventional strategy to fabricate battery electrodes by casting a mixt. of active materials, a nonconductive polymer binder, and a conductive additive onto a metal foil current collector usually leads to electronic or ionic bottlenecks and poor contacts due to the randomly distributed conductive phases.  When high-capacity electrode materials are employed, the high stress generated during electrochem. reactions disrupts the mech. integrity of traditional binder systems, resulting in decreased cycle life of batteries.  Thus, it is crit. to design novel binder systems that can provide robust, low-resistance, and continuous internal pathways to connect all regions of the electrode.  In this Account, we review recent progress on material and structural design of novel binder systems.  Nonconductive polymers with rich carboxylic groups have been adopted as binders to stabilize ultrahigh-capacity inorg. electrodes that experience large vol. or structural change during charge/discharge, due to their strong binding capability to active particles.  To enhance the energy d. of batteries, different strategies have been adopted to design multifunctional binder systems based on conductive polymers because they can play dual functions of both polymeric binders and conductive additives.  We first present that multifunctional binder systems have been designed by tailoring the mol. structures of conductive polymers.  Different functional groups are introduced to the polymeric backbone to enable multiple functionalities, allowing sepd. optimization of the mech. and swelling properties of the binders without detrimental effect on electronic property.  We then describe the design of multifunctional binder systems via rationally controlling their nano- and mol. structures, developing the conductive polymer gel binders with 3D framework nanostructures.  These gel binders provide multiple functions owing to their structure derived properties.  The gel framework facilitates both electronic and ionic transport owing to the continuous pathways for electrons and hierarchical pores for ion diffusion.  The polymer coating formed on every particle acts as surface modification and prevents particle aggregation.  The mech. strong and ductile gel framework also sustains long-term stability of electrodes.  In addn., the structures and properties of gel binders can be facilely tuned.  We further introduce the development of multifunctional binders by hybridizing conductive polymers with other functional materials.  Meanwhile mechanistic understanding on the roles that novel binders play in the electrochem. processes of batteries is also reviewed to reveal general design rules for future binder systems.  We conclude with perspectives on their future development with novel multifunctionalities involved.  Highly efficient binder systems with well-tailored mol. and nanostructures are crit. to reach the entire vol. of the battery and maximize energy use for high-energy and high-power lithium batteries.  We hope this Account promotes further efforts toward synthetic control, fundamental investigation, and application exploration of multifunctional binder materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqbGovia33ojbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljT0CmwCUj2FQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhs1Slu7vO&amp;md5=87c0fcb1d73d1c5246cccd258cb0d74a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.7b00623"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hoshide, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hou, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wane, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ma, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">;                         cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wei; Shen, Fei; Bommier, Clement; Zhu, Hongli; Ji, Xiulei; Hu, Liangbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">231-240</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACHRE4</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0001-4842</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The intermittent nature of renewable energy sources, such as solar and wind, calls for sustainable elec. energy storage (EES) technologies for stationary applications.  Li will be simply too rare for Li-ion batteries (LIBs) to be used for large-scale storage purposes.  In contrast, Na-ion batteries (NIBs) are highly promising to meet the demand of grid-level storage because Na is truly earth abundant and ubiquitous around the globe.  Furthermore, NIBs share a similar rocking-chair operation mechanism with LIBs, which potentially provides high reversibility and long cycling life.  It would be most efficient to transfer knowledge learned on LIBs during the last three decades to the development of NIBs.  Following this logic, rapid progress has been made in NIB cathode materials, where layered metal oxides and polyanionic compds. exhibit encouraging results.  On the anode side, pure graphite as the std. anode for LIBs can only form NaC64 in NIBs if solvent co-intercalation does not occur due to the unfavorable thermodn.  In fact, it was the utilization of a carbon anode in LIBs that enabled the com. successes.  Anodes of metal-ion batteries det. key characteristics, such as safety and cycling life; thus, it is indispensable to identify suitable anode materials for NIBs.In this Account, we review recent development on anode materials for NIBs.  Due to the limited space, we will mainly discuss carbon-based and alloy-based anodes and highlight progress made in our groups in this field.  We first present what is known about the failure mechanism of graphite anode in NIBs.  We then go on to discuss studies on hard carbon anodes, alloy-type anodes, and org. anodes.  Esp., the multiple functions of natural cellulose that is used as a low-cost carbon precursor for mass prodn. and as a soft substrate for tin anodes are highlighted.  The strategies of minimizing the surface area of carbon anodes for improving the first-cycle Coulombic efficiency are also outlined, where graphene oxide was employed as dehydration agent and 2,2,6,6-tetramethylpiperidine-1-oxyl (TEMPO) was used to unzip wood fiber.  Furthermore, surface modification by at. layer deposition technol. is introduced, where we discover that a thin layer of Al2O3 can function to encapsulate Sn nanoparticles, leading to a much enhanced cycling performance.  We also highlight recent work about the phosphorene/graphene anode, which outperformed other anodes in terms of capacity.  The arom. org. anode is also studied as anode with very high initial sodiation capacity.  Furthermore, electrochem. intercalation of Na ions into reduced graphene oxide is applied for fabricating transparent conductors, demonstrating the great feasibility of Na ion intercalation for optical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGorKnQvVSK3P7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljT0CmwCUj2FQ"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1021/acsnano.7b00557</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D11%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D5530-5537%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DA.%2BZhang%26author%3DC.%2BShen%26author%3DQ.%2BLiu%26author%3DX.%2BCao%26author%3DY.%2BMa%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26author%3DC.%2BLau%26author%3DT.-C.%2BChen%26author%3DF.%2BWei%26author%3DC.%2BZhou%26title%3DRed%2BPhosphorus%2BNanodots%2Bon%2BReduced%2BGraphene%2BOxide%2Bas%2Ba%2BFlexible%2Band%2BUltra-Fast%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.7b00557&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.7b08714&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.7b00557&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Red Phosphorus Nanodots on Reduced Graphene Oxide as a Flexible and Ultra-Fast Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yihang; Zhang, Anyi; Shen, Chenfei; Liu, Qingzhou; Cao, Xuan; Ma, Yuqiang; Chen, Liang; Lau, Christian; Chen, Tian-Chi; Wei, Fei; Zhou, Chongwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5530-5537</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries offer an attractive option for potential low cost and large scale energy storage due to the earth abundance of Na.  Red P is considered as a high capacity anode for Na-ion batteries with a theor. capacity of 2596 mA-h/g.  However, similar to Si in Li-ion batteries, several limitations, such as large vol. expansion upon sodiation/desodiation and low electronic conductance, have limited the performance of red P anodes.  To address the above challenges, the authors have developed a method to deposit red P nanodots densely and uniformly onto reduced graphene oxide sheets (P@RGO) to minimize the Na ion diffusion length and the sodiation/desodiation stresses, and the RGO network also serves as electron pathway and creates free space to accommodate the vol. variation of P particles.  The resulted P@RGO flexible anode achieved 1165.4, 510.6, and 135.3 mA-h/g specific charge capacity at 159.4, 31878.9, and 47818.3 mA/g charge/discharge c.d. in rate capability test, and a 914 mA-h/g capacity after 300 deep cycles in cycling stability test at 1593.9 mA/g c.d., which marks a significant performance improvement for red P anodes for Na-ion chem. and flexible power sources for wearable electronics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo9mlp0D8us-rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljT0CmwCUj2FQ"> &gt;&gt; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tian, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Broadwell, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structure Design and Performance Tuning of Nanomaterials for Electrochemical Energy Conversion and Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Acc. Chem. Res.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">49</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2569</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">2577</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.accounts.6b00485</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D49%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D2569-2577%26journal%3DAcc.%2BChem.%2BRes.%26author%3DT.%2BSheng%26author%3DY.%2BXu%26author%3DY.%2BJiang%26author%3DL.%2BHuang%26author%3DN.%2BTian%26author%3DZ.%2BZhou%26author%3DI.%2BBroadwell%26author%3DS.%2BSun%26title%3DStructure%2BDesign%2Band%2BPerformance%2BTuning%2Bof%2BNanomaterials%2Bfor%2BElectrochemical%2BEnergy%2BConversion%2Band%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.accounts.6b00485&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.7b08714&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.accounts.6b00485&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structure Design and Performance Tuning of Nanomaterials for Electrochemical Energy Conversion and Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sheng, Tian; Xu, Yue-Feng; Jiang, Yan-Xia; Huang, Ling; Tian, Na; Zhou, Zhi-You; Broadwell, Ian; Sun, Shi-Gang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2569-2577</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACHRE4</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0001-4842</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review is presented.  The performance of nanomaterials in electrochem. energy conversion (fuel cells) and storage (secondary batteries) strongly depends on the nature of their surfaces.  Designing the structure of electrode materials is the key approach to achieving better performance.  Metal or metal oxide nanocrystals (NCs) with high-energy surfaces and open surface structures have attained significant attention in the past decade since such features possess intrinsically exceptional properties.  However, they are thermodynamically metastable, resulting in a huge challenge in their shape-controlled synthesis.  The tuning of material structure, design, and performance on the nanoscale for electrochem. energy conversion and storage has attracted extended attention over the past few years.  In this Account, recent progress made in shape-controlled synthesis of nanomaterials with high-energy surfaces and open surface structures using both electrochem. methods and surfactant-based wet chem. route are reviewed.In fuel cells, the most important catalytic materials are Pt and Pd and their NCs with high-energy surfaces of convex or concave morphol.  These exhibit remarkable activity toward electrooxidn. of small org. mols., such as formic acid, methanol, and ethanol and so on.  In practical applications, the successful synthesis of Pt NCs with high-energy surfaces of small sizes (sub-10 nm) realized a superior high mass activity.  The electrocatalytic performances have been further boosted by synergetic effects in bimetallic systems, either through surface decoration using foreign metal atoms or by alloying in which the high-index facet structure is preserved and the electronic structure of the NCs is altered.The intrinsic relationship of high electrocatalytic performance dependent on open structure and high-energy surface is also valid for (metal) oxide nanomaterials used in Li ion batteries (LIB).  It is essential for the anode nanomaterials to have optimized structures to keep them more stable during the charge/discharge processes for reducing damaging vol. expansion via intercalation and subsequent reduced battery lifetime.  In the case of cathodes, tuning the surface structure of nanomaterials should be one of the most beneficial strategies to enhance the capacity and rate performance.  In addn., metal oxides with unique defective structure of high catalytic activity and carbon materials of porous structure for facilitating fast Li+ diffusion paths and efficiently trapping polysulfide are most important approached and employed in Li-O2 battery and Li-S battery, resp.  In summary, significant progress has already been made in the electrocatalytic field, and likely emerging techniques based on NCs enclosed with high-energy surfaces and high-index facets could provide a promising platform to investigate the surface structure-catalytic functionality at nanoscale, thus shedding light on the rational design of practical catalysts with high activity, selectivity, and durability for energy conversion and storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqd7PkGuU-WALVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4vaXgvgpXmg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xhs1Kjs7nN&amp;md5=59b9f195b98a65f84e836a8133884982</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1039/c2ee02781j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palomares, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Serras, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Villaluenga, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hueso, K.-B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Carretero-Gonzálezb, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rojo, T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na-Ion Batteries, Recent Advances and Present Challenges to Become Low Cost Energy Storage Systems</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ. Sci.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">5884</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">5901</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c2ee02781j</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2012%26pages%3D5884-5901%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26author%3DV.%2BPalomares%26author%3DP.%2BSerras%26author%3DI.%2BVillaluenga%26author%3DK.-B.%2BHueso%26author%3DJ.%2BCarretero-Gonz%25C3%25A1lezb%26author%3DT.%2BRojo%26title%3DNa-Ion%2BBatteries%252C%2BRecent%2BAdvances%2Band%2BPresent%2BChallenges%2Bto%2BBecome%2BLow%2BCost%2BEnergy%2BStorage%2BSystems%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc2ee02781j&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.7b08714&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc2ee02781j&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-ion batteries, recent advances and present challenges to become low cost energy storage systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Palomares, Veronica; Serras, Paula; Villaluenga, Irune; Hueso, Karina B.; Carretero-Gonzalez, Javier; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5884-5901</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRYtxfVVW_sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4vaXgvgpXmg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Capacity, High-Rate Bi-Sb Alloy Anodes for Lithium-Ion and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Yubao; Manthiram, Arumugam</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

                        cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sb@C coaxial nanotubes as a superior long-life and high-rate anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Zhiming; Yu, Xin-Yao; Lou, Xiong Wen; Paik, Ungyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with a high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1.  However, its practical application is greatly hindered by the rapid capacity fading which is largely due to the large vol. expansion during sodiation.  Tuning the morphol. and structure at the nanoscale or using carbonaceous materials as the buffer layer is essential to address this issue.  Here, a facile carbon-coating coupled with a thermal-redn. strategy has been developed to synthesize unique Sb@C coaxial nanotubes.  With different annealing time, the hollow space and the amt. of Sb inside the tube can be easily tuned by the partial evapn. of Sb.  The as-obtained Sb@C nanotubes exhibit excellent sodium storage properties.  The remarkable electrochem. performance results from the unique coaxial nanoarchitecture.  Specifically, it delivers a high specific capacity of 407 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 240 cycles.  Furthermore, a stable capacity of 240 mAh g-1 can be retained at 1.0 A g-1 even after 2000 cycles.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ab initio characterization of layered MoS2 as anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mortazavi, Majid; Wang, Chao; Deng, Junkai; Shenoy, Vivek B.; Medhekar, Nikhil V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Identifying suitable layered materials as electrodes with desirable electrochem. properties remains a key challenge for rechargeable Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  Using 1st principles methods, here the authors examine the efficacy of layered Mo disulfide (MoS2) as a host electrode material for NIBs.  The authors identify various low energy Na adsorption sites and evaluate the stability of the hexagonal and tetragonal polytypes of MoS2 upon Na intercalation.  The results illustrate a moderately strong binding between Na and MoS2 that is thermodynamically favorable against the cluster formation and phase sepn. of Na.  While Na intercalation in MoS2 results in a phase transformation from the hexagonal phase to the tetragonal phase, it gives rise to a max. theor. capacity of 146 mA-h g-1 and a low av. electrode potential at 0.75-1.25 V.  The calcns. of Na diffusion kinetics indicates a moderately fast mobility of Na in the van der Waals interlayer spaces of MoS2.  These results highlight the promise of MoS2 as an appealing neg. electrode (anode) for rechargeable NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrmkpSdlMDRJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhki9MHruYK-g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXht1WqtbvJ&amp;md5=69c42a444ecaa7ae0b3419398f334c7b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1021/jp410969u"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jing, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cabrera, C.-R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Metallic VS<sub>2</sub> Monolayer: A Promising 2D Anode Material for Lithium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metallic VS2 Monolayer: A Promising 2D Anode Material for Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jing, Yu; Zhou, Zhen; Cabrera, Carlos R.; Chen, Zhongfang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>

                        cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Edge-to-Edge Oriented Self-Assembly of ReS2 Nanoflakes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Qin; Wang, Wenjie; Kong, Xin; Mendes, Rafael G.; Fang, Liwen; Xue, Yinghui; Xiao, Yao; Rummeli, Mark H.; Chen, Shengli; Fu, Lei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The self-assembly of two-dimensional (2D) nanomaterials, an emerging research area, still remains largely unexplored.  The strong interlayer attraction between 2D nanosheets leads to face-to-face stacking rather than edge-to-edge coupling.  We demonstrate, for the first time, how one can induce and control an edge-to-edge self-assembly process for 2D nanomaterials.  The extremely weak van der Waals coupling and strong anisotropy of ReS2 allow us to realize an oriented self-assembly (OSA) process.  The aspect ratio of the resulting ReS2 nanoscrolls can be well controlled.  In addn., we perform simulations to further explain and confirm the OSA process, demonstrating its great potential to be expanded as a general edge-to-edge self-assembly process suitable for other 2D nanomaterials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCAmbc5wp6urVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhki9MHruYK-g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xhtlyqsr7F&amp;md5=987d48b226f419f000feced80f47a71c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201606716"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhuang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Peleckis, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hao, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dou, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Silicene: A Promising Anode for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Adsorption and Diffusion of Lithium on Layered Silicon for Li-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tritsaris, Georgios A.; Kaxiras, Efthimios; Meng, Sheng; Wang, Enge</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The energy d. of Li-ion batteries depends critically on the specific charge capacity of the constituent electrodes.  Silicene, the silicon analog to graphene, being of at. thickness could serve as high-capacity host of Li in Li-ion secondary batteries.  In this work, we employ first-principles calcns. to investigate the interaction of Li with Si in model electrodes of free-standing single-layer and double-layer silicene.  More specifically, we identify strong binding sites for Li, calc. the energy barriers accompanying Li diffusion, and present our findings in the context of previous theor. work related to Li-ion storage in other structural forms of silicon: the bulk and nanowires.  The binding energy of Li is ∼2.2 eV per Li atom and shows small variation with respect to Li content and silicene thickness (one or two layers) while the barriers for Li diffusion are relatively low, typically less than 0.6 eV.  We use our theor. findings to assess the suitability of two-dimensional silicon in the form of silicene layers for Li-ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpFLQuf1Uu1qbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0livbMk9aKIIbQ"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, using solid-state 23Na magic angle spinning NMR and d. functional theory calcn., the authors reveal that MXene Ti3C2Tx in a nonaq. Na+ electrolyte exhibits reversible Na+ intercalation/deintercalation into the interlayer space.  Detailed analyses demonstrate that Ti3C2Tx undergoes expansion of the interlayer distance during the first sodiation, whereby desolvated Na+ is intercalated/deintercalated reversibly.  The interlayer distance is maintained during the whole sodiation/desodiation process due to the pillaring effect of trapped Na+ and the swelling effect of penetrated solvent mols. between the Ti3C2Tx sheets.  Since Na+ intercalation/deintercalation during the electrochem. reaction is not accompanied by any substantial structural change, Ti3C2Tx shows good capacity retention over 100 cycles as well as excellent rate capability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGppfUiN8m8-L7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0livbMk9aKIIbQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xis1GksLc%253D&amp;md5=f66f471d9ba23231889b8a37348dc6b2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201411246"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zeng, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Atomically Thin Arsenene and Antimonene: Semimetal-Semiconductor and Indirect-Direct Band-Gap Transitions</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomically Thin Arsenene and Antimonene: Semimetal-Semiconductor and Indirect-Direct Band-Gap Transitions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Shengli; Yan, Zhong; Li, Yafei; Chen, Zhongfang; Zeng, Haibo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">54</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3112-3115</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The typical two-dimensional (2D) semiconductors MoS2, MoSe2, WS2, WSe2 and black phosphorus have garnered tremendous interest for their unique electronic, optical, and chem. properties.  However, all 2-dimensional semiconductors reported thus far feature band gaps that are smaller than 2.0 eV, which has greatly restricted their applications, esp. in optoelectronic devices with photoresponse in the blue and UV range.  Novel 2-dimensional mono-elemental semiconductors, monolayered arsenene and antimonene, with wide band gaps and high stability were now developed based on 1st-principles calcns.  Although As and Sb are typically semimetals in the bulk, they are transformed into indirect semiconductors with band gaps of 2.49 and 2.28 eV when thinned to one at. layer.  Significantly, under small biaxial strain, these materials were transformed from indirect into direct band-gap semiconductors.  Such dramatic changes in the electronic structure could pave the way for transistors with high on/off ratios, optoelectronic devices working under blue or UV light, and mech. sensors based on new 2-dimensional crystals.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqLPezEkT0D1bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0livbMk9aKIIbQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXivVWrtg%253D%253D&amp;md5=a74d0350f6d18210ad037147bba19766</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201507568"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kan, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zeng, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Semiconducting Group 15 Monolayers: A Broad Range of Band Gaps and High Carrier Mobilities</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-dimensional antimonene single crystals grown by van der Waals epitaxy</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ji, Jianping; Song, Xiufeng; Liu, Jizi; Yan, Zhong; Huo, Chengxue; Zhang, Shengli; Su, Meng; Liao, Lei; Wang, Wenhui; Ni, Zhenhua; Hao, Yufeng; Zeng, Haibo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13352</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Unlike the unstable black phosphorous, another two-dimensional group-VA material, antimonene, was recently predicted to exhibit good stability and remarkable phys. properties.  However, the synthesis of high-quality monolayer or few-layer antimonenes, sparsely reported, has greatly hindered the development of this new field.  Here, we report the van der Waals epitaxy growth of few-layer antimonene monocryst. polygons, their atomical microstructure and stability in ambient condition.  The high-quality, few-layer antimonene monocryst. polygons can be synthesized on various substrates, including flexible ones, via van der Waals epitaxy growth.  Raman spectroscopy and transmission electron microscopy reveal that the obtained antimonene polygons have buckled rhombohedral at. structure, consistent with the theor. predicted most stable β-phase allotrope.  The very high stability of antimonenes was obsd. after aging in air for 30 days.  First-principle and mol. dynamics simulation results confirmed that compared with phosphorene, antimonene is less likely to be oxidized and possesses higher thermodn. stability in oxygen atm. at room temp.  Moreover, antimonene polygons show high elec. cond. up to 104 S m-1 and good optical transparency in the visible light range, promising in transparent conductive electrode applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrIxDPsj_PyHLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0livbMk9aKIIbQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhvVygtrvP&amp;md5=a18d493e12c6521d23fc936e7e928572</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201605407"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Feng, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Epitaxial Growth and Air-Stability of Monolayer Antimonene on PdTe<sub>2</sub></span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Large-scale highly ordered Sb nanorod array anodes with high capacity and rate capability for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Liying; Xu, Yang; Wang, Chengliang; Wen, Liaoyong; Fang, Yaoguo; Mi, Yan; Zhou, Min; Zhao, Huaping; Lei, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2954-2962</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries are a potential substitute to Li-ion batteries for energy storage devices.  However, their poor electrochem. performance, esp. capacity and rate capability, is the major bottleneck to future development.  Here we propose a performance-oriented electrode structure, which is 1D nanostructure arrays with large-scale high ordering, good vertical alignment, and large interval spacing.  Benefiting from these structural merits, a great enhancement in electrochem. performance could be achieved.  Taking Sb as an example, we firstly report large-scale highly ordered Sb nanorod arrays with uniform large interval spacing (190 nm).  In return for this electrode design, high ion accessibility, fast electron transport, and strong electrode integrity are presented here.  Used as additive- and binder-free anodes for Na-ion batteries, Sb nanorod arrays showed a high capacity of 620 mA h g-1 at the 100th cycle with a retention of 84% up to 250 cycles at 0.2 A g-1, and a superior rate capability for delivering reversible capacities of 579.7 and 557.7 mA h g-1 at 10 and 20 A g-1, resp.  A full cell coupled by a P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 cathode and a Sb nanorod array anode was also constructed, which showed good cycle performance up to 250 cycles, high rate capability up to 20 A g-1, and large energy d. up to 130 Wh kg-1.  These excellent electrochem. performances shall pave the way for developing more applications of Sb nanorod arrays in energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpRS7y0VfakjLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljeJmE0U9liMg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFGns7nO&amp;md5=50b74924c2a93cc137e8a9993ce641fa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1039/c2cc32730a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ai, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Capacity Na-Storage and Superior Cyclability of Nanocomposite Sb/C Anode for Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Better Cycling Performances of Bulk Sb in Na-Ion Batteries Compared to Li-Ion Systems: An Unexpected Electrochemical Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Darwiche, Ali; Marino, Cyril; Sougrati, Moulay T.; Fraisse, Bernard; Stievano, Lorenzo; Monconduit, Laure</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">134</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20805-20811</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa).  In addn., fluoroethylene carbonate added to the electrolyte combined with an appropriate electrode formulation based on CM-cellulose, carbon black, and vapor ground carbon fibers seems to be determinant in the excellent performances of this material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfZ6rvnJyfxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljeJmE0U9liMg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhslCgsbnE&amp;md5=75362e7708fe6434655290ce0aa7cac0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2014.07.034"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huh, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">X-ray Diffraction of Multi-Layer Graphenes: Instant Measurement and Determination of the Number of Layers</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Carbon</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">78</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">617</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">621</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">X-ray diffraction of multi-layer graphenes: Instant measurement and determination of number of layers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huh, Seung Hun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A method for detg. the no. of layers (NL) or thickness (DGP) of multi-layer graphene (MLG) using X-ray diffraction (XRD) is reported for the first time.  The XRD pattern showed clear variations in the full-width-at-half-max. (FWHM) values of the (0 0 2) peak of cryst. MLG with NL = 3, 4, 5, 6, and 7.  The large FWHM difference per layer and the instant measurement of large areas of MLG demonstrates that XRD is a powerful probe.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Real-time observation of graphene layer growth: Coupling of the interlayer spacing with thickness</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Daming; Gao, Hui; Zhang, Xingmin; Yang, Tieying; Li, Li; Yin, Guangzhi; Li, Xiuhong; Nicklin, Chris; Gao, Xingyu; Li, Zhong; Yi, Lin; Li, Xiaolong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In-situ two-dimensional grazing incidence X-ray diffraction was applied in isothermal growth of graphene on nickel through chem. vapor deposition.  The analyses showed that the graphene interlayer spacing decreases with the increasing no. of graphene layers (growth time increase).  Moreover, the as-deposited graphene can be gradually removed through in-situ Ar annealing treatment and inverse interlayer spacing change was also obsd., i.e., the interlayer spacing of graphene increases with the no. of graphene layers decrease.  These results prove that there is a strong coupling effect between the interlayer spacing and the no. of graphene layers.  The weak interlayer interactions between graphene layers and the interface effects may contribute to this phenomenon.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpuMInkWgXS47Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljeJmE0U9liMg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXht1elurzP&amp;md5=afe8dc93b2e9f8304e2c8e1d513572ee</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201505918"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Double-Walled Sb@TiO<sub>2–x</sub> Nanotubes as A Superior High-Rate and Ultralong-Lifespan Anode Material for Na-Ion and Li-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Double-Walled Sb@TiO2-x Nanotubes as a Superior High-Rate and Ultralong-Lifespan Anode Material for Na-Ion and Li-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Nana; Bai, Zhongchao; Qian, Yitai; Yang, Jian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Here, double-walled cryst. Sb@amorphous TiO2-x nanotubes are synthesized by the calcination of Sb2S3@TiO2 nanorods in Ar/H2 produced by the hydrolysis of tetra-Bu titanate (TBOT) on Sb2S3 nanorods.  The formation of the double-walled structures could be assigned to the facile redn. of Sb2S3 and the strong interaction of Sb to TiO2.  Such a structure accommodates the vol. variation upon cycling well, then keeps the structure stable.  Meanwhile, this calcination in Ar/H2 also generates a lot of oxygen vacancies in the shell, supported by Ti3+ species in XPS spectra.  They would enhance the charge-transfer kinetics, particularly at the interface.  Thus, the double-walled nanotubes show excellent electrochem. performance as an anode material in the lithium-ion batteries and in sodium-ion batteries, both of which are on the top of the reported list.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrrrdrYefF6qrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj16Zd7JTqDdA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjtlKms7Y%253D&amp;md5=0bb077f676824aae644f1f5f12368294</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1088/2053-1583/2/1/011002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Island, J.-O.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Steele, G.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Direct Superassemblies of Freestanding Metal-Carbon Frameworks Featuring Reversible Crystalline-Phase Transformation for Electrochemical Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kong, Biao; Zu, Lianhai; Peng, Chengxin; Zhang, Yan; Zhang, Wei; Tang, Jing; Selomulya, Cordelia; Zhang, Liudi; Chen, Hanxing; Wang, Yang; Liu, Yang; He, Haili; Wei, Jing; Lin, Xiaocheng; Luo, Wei; Yang, Jianping; Zhao, Zaiwang; Liu, Yong; Yang, Jinhu; Zhao, Dongyuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">138</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">50</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">16533-16541</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-power sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with long-term cycling attract increasing attention for large-scale energy storage.  However, traditional SIBs toward practical applications still suffer from low rate capability and poor cycle induced by pulverization and amorphorization of anodes at high rate (over 5 C) during the fast ion insertion/extn. process.  The present work demonstrates a robust strategy for a variety of (Sb-C, Bi-C, Sn-C, Ge-C, Sb-Bi-C) freestanding metal-carbon framework thin films via a space-confined superassembly (SCSA) strategy.  The sodium-ion battery employing the Sb-C framework exhibits an unprecedented performance with a high specific capacity of 246 mAh/g, long life cycle (5000 cycles), and superb capacity retention (almost 100%) at a high rate of 7.5 C (3.51A/g).  Further investigation indicates that the unique framework structure enables unusual reversible cryst.-phase transformation, guaranteeing the fast and long-cyclability sodium storage.  This study may open an avenue to developing long-cycle-life and high-power SIBs for practical energy applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqK5sMN8Rb52rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj16Zd7JTqDdA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitVCjsb7P&amp;md5=37b51d2617e79080500d7a0178354f67</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1039/C5NR02578H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Peng, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Peng, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huo, K.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bamboo Leaf Derived Ultrafine Si Nanoparticles and Si/C Nanocomposites for High-Performance Li-Ion Battery Anodes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">13840</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">13847</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bamboo leaf derived ultrafine Si nanoparticles and Si/C nanocomposites for high-performance Li-ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Lei; Gao, Biao; Peng, Changjian; Peng, Xiang; Fu, Jijiang; Chu, Paul K.; Huo, Kaifu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">33</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13840-13847</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2040-3372</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Silicon-based nanomaterials are promising anode materials in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) due to their high theor. capacity of 4200 mA h g-1, more than 10 times that of com. graphite.  Si nanoparticles (NPs) with a diam. of or below 10 nm generally exhibit enhanced lithium storage properties due to their small size and large surface area.  However, it is challenging to generate such ultrafine Si NPs by a facile and scalable method.  This paper reports a scalable method to fabricate ultrafine Si NPs 5-8 nm in size from dead bamboo leaves (BLs) by thermally decompg. the org. matter, followed by magnesiothermic redn. in the presence of NaCl as a heat scavenger.  The ultrafine Si NPs show a high capacity of 1800 mA h g-1 at a 0.2 C (1 C = 4200 mA g-1) rate and are thus promising anode materials in lithium-ion batteries.  To achieve better rate capability, the BLs-derived ultrafine Si NPs are coated with a thin amorphous carbon layer (Si@C) and then dispersed and embedded in a reduced graphene oxide (RGO) network to produce Si@C/RGO nanocomposites by a layer-by-layer assembly method.  The double protection rendered by the carbon shell and RGO network synergistically yield structural stability, high elec. cond. and a stable solid electrolyte interface during Li insertion/extn.  The Si@C/RGO nanocomposites show excellent battery properties with a high capacity of 1400 mA h g-1 at a high c.d. of 2 C and remarkable rate performance with a capacity retention of 60% when the c.d. is increased 20 times from 0.2 to 4 C.  This work provides a simple, low cost, and scalable approach enabling the use of BL waste as a sustainable source for the prodn. of ultrafine Si NPs towards high-performance LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCVZYXBQPBf7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj16Zd7JTqDdA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXptFCmtb0%253D&amp;md5=6546c8c079c59544d0cececd0b1da742</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2010.12.101"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lv, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">NuLi, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrodeposited Porous-Microspheres Li-Si Films as Negative Electrodes in Lithium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Stable Li-ion battery anodes by in-situ polymerization of conducting hydrogel to conformally coat silicon nanoparticles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu Hui; Yu Guihua; Pan Lijia; Liu Nian; McDowell Matthew T; Bao Zhenan; Cui Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1943</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Silicon has a high-specific capacity as an anode material for Li-ion batteries, and much research has been focused on overcoming the poor cycling stability issue associated with its large volume changes during charging and discharging processes, mostly through nanostructured material design.  Here we report incorporation of a conducting polymer hydrogel into Si-based anodes: the hydrogel is polymerized in-situ, resulting in a well-connected three-dimensional network structure consisting of Si nanoparticles conformally coated by the conducting polymer.  Such a hierarchical hydrogel framework combines multiple advantageous features, including a continuous electrically conductive polyaniline network, binding with the Si surface through either the crosslinker hydrogen bonding with phytic acid or electrostatic interaction with the positively charged polymer, and porous space for volume expansion of Si particles.  With this anode, we demonstrate a cycle life of 5,000 cycles with over 90% capacity retention at current density of 6.0 A g(-1).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcRUksfu_AqPfJQHPYJuLg8TfW6udTcc2eZ6zX6qeUnDl7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3snpsVamsg%253D%253D&amp;md5=af8b5d797c24a13f3d6b450e152b3134</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms5033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">He, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Matsuda, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cumings, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Expanded Graphite as Superior Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Expanded graphite as superior anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wen, Yang; He, Kai; Zhu, Yujie; Han, Fudong; Xu, Yunhua; Matsuda, Isamu; Ishii, Yoshitaka; Cumings, John; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4033</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite, as the most common anode for com. Li-ion batteries, has been reported to have a very low capacity when used as a Na-ion battery anode.  It is well known that electrochem. insertion of Na+ into graphite is significantly hindered by the insufficient interlayer spacing.  Here we report expanded graphite as a Na-ion battery anode.  Prepd. through a process of oxidn. and partial redn. on graphite, expanded graphite has an enlarged interlayer lattice distance of 4.3 Å yet retains an analogous long-range-ordered layered structure to graphite.  In situ transmission electron microscopy has demonstrated that the Na-ion can be reversibly inserted into and extd. from expanded graphite.  Galvanostatic studies show that expanded graphite can deliver a high reversible capacity of 284 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 20 mA g-1, maintain a capacity of 184 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, and retain 73.92% of its capacity after 2,000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFEZ8wJYk1irVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhfR5UL92qoKg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksVeqs7g%253D&amp;md5=e4bc2edac8d22121e7986e165b7df007</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.82.125416"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Persson, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hinuma, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Meng, Y.-S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Van der Ven, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ceder, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Thermodynamic and Kinetic Properties of the Li-Graphite from First-Principles Calculations</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Phys. </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yi, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title"><i>In Situ</i> Observation of Thermal Proton Transport through Graphene Layers</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">11</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">8970</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">8977</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsnano.7b03359</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D11%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D8970-8977%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DD.%2BZhu%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BGao%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DR.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BXu%26author%3DG.%2BJi%26author%3DS.%2BJiang%26author%3DB.%2BZhao%26author%3DG.%2BYin%26author%3DL.%2BLi%26author%3DT.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26author%3DL.%2BYi%26author%3DX.%2BLi%26title%3DIn%2BSitu%2BObservation%2Bof%2BThermal%2BProton%2BTransport%2Bthrough%2BGraphene%2BLayers%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.7b03359&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.7b08714&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.7b03359&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ observation of thermal proton transport through graphene layers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Daming; Liu, Xing; Gao, Yi; Li, Yadong; Wang, Rui; Xu, Zijian; Ji, Gengwu; Jiang, Sheng; Zhao, Bin; Yin, Guangzhi; Li, Li; Yang, Tieying; Wang, Yong; Yi, Lin; Li, Xiaolong; Tai, Renzhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8970-8977</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Protons can penetrate through single-layer graphene, but thicker graphene layers (more than 2 layers), which possess more compact electron d., are thought to be unfavorable for penetration by protons at room temp. and elevated temps.  In this work, we developed an in situ subsecond time-resolved grazing-incidence X-ray diffraction technique, which fully realizes the real-time observation of the thermal proton interaction with the graphene layers at high temp.  By following the evolution of interlayer structure during the protonation process, we demonstrated that thermal protons can transport through multilayer graphene (more than 8 layers) on nickel foil at 900 °C.  In comparison, under the same conditions, the multilayer graphenes are impermeable to argon, nitrogen, helium, and their derived ions.  Complementary in situ transport measurements simultaneously verify the penetration phenomenon at high temp.  Moreover, the direct transport of protons through graphene is regarded as the dominant contribution to the penetration phenomenon.  The thermal activation, weak interlayer interaction between layers, and the affinity of the nickel catalyst may all contribute to the proton transport.  We believe that this method could become one of the established approaches for the characterization of the ions intercalated with 2D materials in situ and in real-time.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqtGG9owotkirVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhfR5UL92qoKg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXht12mt7bJ&amp;md5=6f4ee13e40e62f327f78aac4980b704e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.7b08320"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tai, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yi, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Construction of Novel 3-Dimensional Graphene/Amorphous Porous Carbon Hybrids with Enhanced Lithium Storage Properties</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                             cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.53.R10441"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ordejón, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Artacho, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Soler, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Self-Consistent Order-N Density-Functional Calculations for Very Large Systems</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Phys.
